        <a href="/review/show/924563645?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23591855-viji-sarath-bookish-endeavors" class="user" title="Viji Sarath (Bookish endeavors)">Viji Sarath (Bookish endeavors)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1305986.Blood_Oath" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780449203910" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/23591855-viji-sarath-bookish-endeavors?shelf=detective-spy-thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">detective-spy-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer924563645">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12421976864875206981">Old wine in new bottle.. Well.. I shouldn't say new since I've seen other writers do it in a better way.. It's a polished bottle.. <br />Pete Houston visits France to look for his father's grave,the father whom he had never known. His wife is with him and because of some twists that take place when he tries to find out about his father,she gets killed. He is determined to find out her killer and is helped by Simone,the daughter of the owner of the hotel where he is staying. And they find out a 37-year</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12421976864875206981">Old wine in new bottle.. Well.. I shouldn't say new since I've seen other writers do it in a better way.. It's a polished bottle.. <br />Pete Houston visits France to look for his father's grave,the father whom he had never known. His wife is with him and because of some twists that take place when he tries to find out about his father,she gets killed. He is determined to find out her killer and is helped by Simone,the daughter of the owner of the hotel where he is staying. And they find out a 37-year old secret.. <br />As the story progresses,we feel that it's something huge that's going to happen. There is all this tension and secrecy and shadowing. And when you get the whole picture,you feel like-that's it.?!! And the stunts in this book is like some small-town fight. It doesn't do justice to the 'real bad' image of the villains. <br />Altogether,this book doesn't have a plot of its own and the author has failed miserably in his attempt to present it in a descent manner. <br />PS:- <br />I saw Stephen King's praise for this novel on the cover page,"best selling thriller-packed with tension" and was lured into reading it. And now I've decided never to read the praises. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1023937224">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1023937224" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12877676-martin-hill" class="left imgcol" title="Martin Hill"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442643248p2/12877676.jpg" alt="Martin Hill" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1023937224?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 18, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12877676-martin-hill" class="user" title="Martin Hill">Martin Hill</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1305986.Blood_Oath" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780449203910" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1023937224">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17374633367271827054">Peter Houston, an American novelist, travels to France to pay homage to the father he never knew, an American soldier killed in action in the weeks following the Normandy invasion. When he discovers there is no record of his father being buried in any of the American war cemeteries, Houston begins looking for a Frenchman who promised the writer's mother he would look after the dead soldier's grave. Houston's search threatens to uncover long buried secrets, and suddenly finds Houston targeted by</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17374633367271827054">Peter Houston, an American novelist, travels to France to pay homage to the father he never knew, an American soldier killed in action in the weeks following the Normandy invasion. When he discovers there is no record of his father being buried in any of the American war cemeteries, Houston begins looking for a Frenchman who promised the writer's mother he would look after the dead soldier's grave. Houston's search threatens to uncover long buried secrets, and suddenly finds Houston targeted by unknown forces. Those forces make one deadly mistake, they kill the woman Houston loves and when he swear a blood oath, Houston turns from being the hunted to being the hunter.<br /><br />David Morrell's <em>Blood Oath</em> is a classic Hitchcockian mystery; that is, a story about an ordinary man who innocently becomes embroiled in deadly enigma and is forced to take action to save himself and those he loves. One can almost imagine Cary Grant as Houston. And like a good Hitchcock movie, Blood Oath soon turns from mystery to thrilling suspense. <br /><br />Beyond the mystery and suspense, however, this is also the story about a boy who grows up without his father. Father-son relations often play a part in Morrell's novels, and none more than Blood Oath. As Morrell explains in the forward, he grew up never knowing his father, a Canadian pilot who was killed in WWII. Like Houston, Morrell began a search to learn more about the man, a search that eventually led him to a war grave in the United Kingdom. While reading <em>Blood Oath</em>, it wasn't difficult to hear Morrell's childhood pain in Houston's childhood angst.<br /><br />In the end, <em>Blood Oath</em> is a fine mystery thriller, one of Morrell's best.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17374633367271827054">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1436782630152461468">Imagine going to France to visit your father's grave and find he isn't burried there? <br />Pete Houston never knew his dad but when his mother died he goes to France to visit the grave of his father and tell him about his wife but his father's not there.<br />All Pete and his wife have is info that Pierre de StLaurnet wrote to Pete's mom and promised to look after his fathers' grave but when they investigate, St. Laurent is also missing.<br />A stranger tells Pete that St. Laurent lives in another town but when</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1436782630152461468">Imagine going to France to visit your father's grave and find he isn't burried there? <br />Pete Houston never knew his dad but when his mother died he goes to France to visit the grave of his father and tell him about his wife but his father's not there.<br />All Pete and his wife have is info that Pierre de StLaurnet wrote to Pete's mom and promised to look after his fathers' grave but when they investigate, St. Laurent is also missing.<br />A stranger tells Pete that St. Laurent lives in another town but when traveling there, a van forces Pete's car off the road. They crash into a river, Pete escapes, his wife, Jan, does not.<br />Pete awakens in the hotel where the authorities had taken him. The owner and his daughter, Simone, permitted Pete to recover there.<br />Upon recovering and taking care of his wife's funeral, Simone takes Peter to the address he had been given for St. Laurent but this too is a setup.<br />They return to the military cemetary where he thought his father was burried and find that two other people came to find there family member in the same situation, and found their loved one's weren't burried there either.<br />Morrell does a find job in keeping the suspense going. How Houston could continue so soon after his wife died and was cremated was improbable but the rest of the story went well. The characters were well drawn and the story told dramatically.<br />The main character has been compared to Robert Ludlum's Jason Bourne and I think there could be a valid comparison.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79512314">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9010690732066655564">Creative Plotting. During WWII, a squad of soldiers goes MIA during a battle in France. Not long after, Peter Houston's mom (wife to one of the soldiers) gets a letter from a Frenchman. The letter promises he will maintain the father's grave as a gesture of gratitude for the sacrifice he made in behalf of France and the free world. Thirty-two years later, Peter travels to France to visit his father's grave. No grave. He searches for the man who wrote the letter, he's disappeared, too. With a lit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9010690732066655564">Creative Plotting. During WWII, a squad of soldiers goes MIA during a battle in France. Not long after, Peter Houston's mom (wife to one of the soldiers) gets a letter from a Frenchman. The letter promises he will maintain the father's grave as a gesture of gratitude for the sacrifice he made in behalf of France and the free world. Thirty-two years later, Peter travels to France to visit his father's grave. No grave. He searches for the man who wrote the letter, he's disappeared, too. With a little investigation,Peter discovers that the families of each of the MIA squad members received a similar letter from the Frenchman, and that no grave exists for any of the soldiers. Peter resolves to get to the bottom of the mystery, and thus begins a chaotic series of events. The writing in the shoot'em up in the last few pages is a bit over the top. Otherwise, not a bad story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9010690732066655564">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/24303945-hana?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1267240211">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14279136328012645757">Gow can an innocent idea change your life - you wish to find your father's grave and suddenly you are hunted, your wife is murdered and you find out that your father not only lives but is a member of a mob. It was a good thriller with fast pace, good writing and interesting chararcters. I liked it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1055277074">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055277074" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8876280-stephen" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1349271646p2/8876280.jpg" alt="Stephen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1055277074?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 05, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8876280-stephen" class="user" title="Stephen">Stephen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1055277074">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16982311206233483803">Not a bad book, but certainly not one of Morrell's masterpieces. This bit of 80's fiction follows the running through the French country jumping fences, dodging trees, and trying to get away while searching for answers paradigm. This book could easily be overlooked without much loss. If you like Morrell, go read The Brotherhood of the Rose series, The Fifth profession, Creepers, Scavenger, or even Testament.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer562257248">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4282057315968269899">4.5 stars.<br /><br />On the book cover is a quote from Stephen King, "I defy readers not to finish this novel in a single sitting." If I hadn't started so late in the day yesterday, I would have, I couldn't put it down. Liked the writing better than the earlier books and will continue to read them, somewhat in order.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_187628195">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187628195" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5547564-david" class="left imgcol" title="David"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1354549178p2/5547564.jpg" alt="David" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/187628195?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 23, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5547564-david" class="user" title="David">David</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1305986.Blood_Oath" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780449203910" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer187628195">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7777941783911742599">Taut, relentless thriller from genre master David Morrell. This is one of his early works and suffers at times from melodrama, but not enough to be distracting. I can't speak for other editions, but the first edition hardcover has no fewer than three typos. Sloppy editing aside, an enjoyable book.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/vIG6wUtSJrfewY4jl5a56uDMqZaQ/tZIz00FAwbrlGbJjk49/9cYFOjcoPwP7xV4nTxvxOevPNJNDGGwI5YFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12535.David_Morrell">About David Morrell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/12535.David_Morrell"><img alt="12535" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1218135781p2/12535.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5919236847879832134">David Morrell is a Canadian novelist from Kitchener, Ontario, who has been living in the United States for a number of years. He is best known for his debut 1972 novel <em>First Blood</em>, which would later become a successful film franchise starring Sylvester Stallone. More recently, he has been writing the <em>Captain America</em> comic books limited-series <em>The Chosen</em>.</span>

    </div>
